Therefore, my children, since I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the knowledge in medicine, by completing it you will attain its end, and by reading its explanations and clarifications, I find that I should complete this treatise on surgery for you.
Since the art of surgery is almost entirely obsolete in our kingdom and time, due to the great danger it poses, and the instruments of surgery are lost; only a few small descriptions remain in the books of the ancients, which have been corrupted by many errors and hazards until their meanings are obscured and their power diminished.
I find it appropriate to arrange this treatise according to the method of explanation and clarification and abbreviation; and so that the forms of cautery instruments and other tools of the work come with their explanations and preparation, which is necessary.
One reason for the scarcity of good craftsmen in this field is that the art of medicine requires lengthy study, and the one who practices it must have knowledge of anatomy, which includes knowing the joints and shapes of members, their connection and separation; having knowledge of bones, nerves and ligaments, and their number, and the extraction of them; and of the pulsating veins and quiet ones, and the locations for their incision.
And as Hippocrates said, a word is a small thing in itself, but it has great significance in work and especially in the art of the hand.
And we have already said about this in the introduction of this book; whoever is not well-versed in anatomy is not qualified to avoid falling into error, which can lead to the death of men, as I have seen many of these people, some are ignorant of this science and abandon it after their learning and experience.
I saw a foolish and experienced doctor make an abscess called scrophulus on the neck of a woman, and he cut some arteries in her neck so that a large amount of blood flowed until the woman died among them.
I also saw another doctor who believed he could pull out a stone from a man in his condition, and the stone was large, and it came to him and cut a piece of the bladder while pulling out the stone, so that the man died on the third day.
I have already stated that this is the case, and I saw that due to the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, it was clear that he would die.
I also saw another doctor who received a salary from a duke of our land to perform surgery, and he went to a black castellan who was owed a fracture in his thigh; and the doctor prepared himself with his ignorance, extracted the fracture, on the wound, with pulvines and splints of strong construction, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
He laid it open as desired, and he applied the dressing, and he left it to heal for several days and commanded us to remove the bandages; and so it was until the thigh and leg became abscessed, and this led to ruin.
And you are called upon to him, and prepare to unbind the liniment, and peace and quiet is obtained, and he may then alleviate his pains.
However, corruption had already spread in the limb, so it could not be restrained, and the corruption continued to spread through the limb until the patient was at risk.
And another doctor pierced an abscess full of cancer, and it became an ulcer close to several days, until the evil within it was magnified by its lord.
The cause is that the cancerous growth is pure of melancholy humor, and therefore it should not come upon him with all ferocity, but rather on an organ or member that is most vulnerable to it.
And for this reason, my son, it is necessary that the operation be divided into two parts: one part is the operation associated with health, and the other part is the operation in which danger lies in greater decisions.
And I have already examined this matter in every place of this book where the operation is carried out with error and fear; therefore it is necessary for you to guard against this and let go of that, so that foolish people do not find a way to speak and mislead you.

Gualla now says in some of her teachings: "Do not treat an evil disease, so that bad doctors do not become known."

Therefore I say that the speech about the quality of the juxtaposition of the cautery and its negative effects is a long, detailed, subtle discourse full of science, hidden secrets; and many wise people have already spoken at length about it, and they disagree, and to me it amounts to only a small part of their discourses, fearing prolixity.
And therefore I say that the use of cauterization applies universally to all matters or substances, with two exceptions, which are situations without matter.
In the situation without matter and dry, there is disagreement; for some say that cauterization is beneficial in this case, while others say the opposite, that cauterization is not suitable for a disease that is due to quality and dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and it is appropriate that a dry and desiccated disease be treated with wet things.
And I say that he who says the opposite is correct, that cauterization is beneficial in all dry and desiccated diseases that occur in the bodies of men, because when you compare the bodies of men and their humidity to the nature of fire, the bodies of men are burned by it.
And I say from experience that this has been observed in some cases by me.
However, it is not necessary to reiterate that which has already been expounded and exercised in the chapter on cauterization by previous exercise, and to know the diversity of human bodies and the disposition of diseases in their bodies, and the causes of these diseases, and the accidents associated with them, and the time span of these conditions.
However, in other situations, there is no need for fear, and especially in wet and cold diseases, because all doctors agree on these, and there is no disagreement about the beneficial effects of cauterization in these cases.
And you, my sons, know that the secret of healing by cauterization with fire and the goodness of it is that cauterization with burning medicine is superior to cauterization with fire, because fire is simple, its action does not extend beyond the member being cauterized and is harmful only to a small extent to neighboring members.
However, the action of burning medicine extends to adjacent members, and it has a strong effect in bringing disease to the diseased member that is difficult to heal and causes pain.
But fire, because of its sublimity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, except that it superfluesc. Know, sons, that they disagree about the time in which it is appropriate to perform cautery and pause the best time of springtime.
I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm due to accidental time is submerged in the benefit of what is drawn from cautery, and especially if the cautery is for pain or necessary pain, which do not tolerate delay, since it is feared that the harm coming from malicious intent, which is greater than small harm entering through time, could overcome it.
Do not believe in your thoughts, or sons, that it is not considered except by the common people and foolish doctors, because reduction of that disease which is cured by cautery is not complete at all times, and they pause on this consequence.
And the cause is not as they believe, because cautery is not simply in a place of medicine that alters the complexion and dries up the humidities that are the cause of pain.
But indeed, cautery surpasses medicine due to the desire for its value and virtue in its operation and the greatness of its Lord.
It is possible that the disease will return at some hour of time, according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease, as well as its power, and what is prepared in his body from accumulations in him of superfluities and humidities, and what is obtained for him in food and similar things from these causes; except that the disease in which cautery is administered is a subtle disease in a member with few superfluities and humidities, such as cautionery on teeth for pain, it is possible that the pain will not return there, but rather it is done in small amounts.

And the cause is opposite of that; and my intention that cautery is the last remedy of medicine is not because it is administered in some diseases when methods of healing do not confer, but rather at the end of the disease, cautionery is administered and improves upon it. Now you understand that cautery is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the intention that I understand from the common people and the follies of foolish doctors.
They said the ancients that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
They said that the location of cautery does not harm, as this is not absolutely true, because I already have it proven and observed that it does not do so in some bodies, and cauterizing with gold is better than with iron as they say; however, when you perform cauterization with fire from gold, it is not declared to you, because it depends on the quantity that you want according to the roughness of gold, and it prepares to receive cold; and if you adjust it above the fire, the gold melts due to heat, and if some layers occur in the fire for the craftsman to cut through the occupation of that.
And because of this, cautery with iron must be done lightly and more carefully in terms of operation.

The first chapter.

And be careful not to expose the bone because the patient will experience great pain different from the pain of all other head cauterizations.

Chapter VI:
Chapter on Cauterization for Torticollis (Wryneck).
Wryneck that is cured with cauterization is only done for the species that come from poison, as mentioned in the divisions of diseases.
Cauterization should be avoided for the species that enter by dryness or spasm of the nerve.
If the treatment of wryneck with herbs, capers, and gargles does not work, you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: first, make an incision in the ear, second, apply a small hot iron to the temple, and third, cauterize the junction of the lips.
Allow the cautery to cool in the opposite direction of the affected side, as the healing process will only occur in the healthy area.
The method of cauterization involves using the cautery to make an incision in the upper part of the ear near the corner of the head, and another incision along the temple, the length of which should be the same as the width of the finger used to make it. After making the incisions, allow the cautery to cool before proceeding with treatment. Ensure that the cauterization is carried out until the affected area is completely burned away.
And this is the shape of the cautery, it is the specialized tool of the blacksmith, its shape being like a tabletop. However, it is more subtle than what one can see with the eyes; and it is necessary to remove any excess thickness from it.
Then take care of the place with what is in front of the process before it heals.

Chapter XVIII.
Treatise on the Cauterization of Fissures in the Feet.

And a line is drawn that goes along the long side of the wound and above it, and another line at the top; then lay your hand on the rupture with one heated iron, but the first cautery should be lighter and better.
Chapter 46.
On cauterization of twisting (worms).
When a wound occurs in some body part by accident or blow and the pain persists for a long time without being cured with medicines, then it is necessary to cauterize it with a pointed cautery.
The cautery should be of all body parts according to its size and smallness, as well as the strength and effectiveness of it, and the location of twisting and pain of it.
If it is healed by the first cautery, that is good; otherwise, continue to cauterize it; because it is customary for those pains to be punctured in a body part near the affected one, so it is necessary to achieve that with cauterization until the patient is cured.
Chapter 47.
On cauterization of leprosy.
Some types of leprosy are observed to be cured by cauterization, especially the type that is caused by the corruption of phlegm and melancholy.
Therefore, when you want to cauterize it, consider if the leprosy is common and can be cured with what we have said in the division (of the text) and not deny or doubt, nor is it present, and fear that corruption may affect the entire body of the patient and his complexion, then cauterize it on the head with 5 cauterizations: one in the middle of the forehead, one below it, turn the face to the end of the hair; one on each ear; and one behind, on the nape or neck.
Lastly, place your hand on the cautery a little away from where there is slight pressure on the bone, and thus the scabs are moved, so that the expulsion of thick vapors is alleviated; then cauterize it on the sole as previously prescribed.
If the leprosy has already spread over the patient and appears manifestly, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned on the head; on the tip of the nose, and two cauterizations on both cheeks, and two on both shoulders, and 6 cauterizations on the spine, and a large one near the backbone, and one on the coccyx, and two on each ankle, and one on each heel, and 2 on each elbow, and one on each wrist, and 2 on each finger joint, and on each toe joint, and on all the joints of his hands and feet, and on each tendon of his limbs; then cauterize it over all the joints of the aforementioned parts, and on each talon of his feet, and on the phalanges of his toes.
And be careful not to burn the nerves that are over the heel (talon).
Sometimes it is cauterized with a single cautery on the bone of the penis and another on the mouth of the stomach, and another on the liver.
You should know that the more cauterizations you make, the more beneficial it is and the faster the healing; you should also know that the patient does not feel pain in the cautery, as has been said, because the body of the patient is already numb.
It is necessary that the cauterizations be large or few depending on the body parts and joints according to the characteristics of the tools (used).
Care for the cautery with flour of eggs beaten with honey and the other treatment until it is healed.
Chapter 48.
On cauterization of numbness (paralysis).
When some body part is paralyzed or numb and cured with medicines, oils, and plasters, but not healed, then you cauterize the paralyzed member with cauteries according to the size of the body part or its smallness.
Let your cautery enter the intestine a little. Approach care for that which is swallowed until it heals.
At certain times, some paralysis is cauterized that affects the limbs and feet, the spine of the back and causes numbness in the nerves that affect that member, and the paralysis is relieved.
However, do not presume this unless one is skilled in the anatomy of the members and the exit of the nerves throughout the entire body moving them.
Chapter 49.
On cauterization of ulcers that are morphous.
When ulcers are old and do not respond to any of the swallowed medicines, then you cauterize over it with a cautery, using a small amount of the substance according to the size of the wound until its whiteness and color is removed, and its color is changed.
Approach care for that which is made of errors and lentils with roasted oil and fennel leaves, and pigeon or hare blood, each one is divided and all are mixed, and let a strip be sewn over it until healed.
Chapter 1.
On cauterization of cancer.
When cancer begins and you want to remove it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it as it is rotated.
The wise ones say that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle position; however, I have not seen this, because I fear that it may be ulcerated, and I have seen this several times.
It is therefore correct that it should be cauterized in a circular manner as we have said, or with multiple cauteries.
Chapter 11.
On cauterization of adubilati.
If an adubilati is delayed in ripening, either due to the excess or the condition of the patient, who is old and decrepit, with little blood, or by time, and you want to hasten the ripening of adubilati; then cauterize it in a circular manner with multiple small puncture cauteries, and apply leeches to it so that it will ripen quickly.
However, if you want to perform perforation with cautery, then heat the cautery whose shape is as follows, and place it in the middle of the adubilati until it penetrates the wound.
And if the cautery is placed in that location which is below, to relieve the body of the arm; then care for it until healed.
Chapter 12.
Of cauterization by corrosion.
Corrosion is decay that spreads in the member, which consumes it like fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you see that decay in a location that requires cauterization with fire, then you should make small and large hot coals as appropriate for that location where the decay is present.
And cauterize it entirely over all parts, so that you exterminate all decay and there remains no cause for it.
Leave it for three days, and keep pressure over the cauterized areas with oil mixed in, until all scars are healed and all corruption is exterminated.
And apply cure to that with tender meat-producing flesh.
However, if after three days the flesh born is healthy and there is no corruption, that's good; however, otherwise, repeat the cauterization over what has rotted in the corrupt locations.
Decay is treated with certain medications at times because it is a medium for cauterization. However, cauterizing with fire is of little help in healing.
And as I have already said, the cure for it with sharp medicine should be taken when necessary.
Chapter XXXIII.
Cauterization by nails and similar things.
Observed in the feet of patients suffering from what is called a nail (claw), which is large, deep-rooted, and penetrates the foot; and cauterization for these is performed in two ways: either by fire or water boil.
However, caution with fire is that you make a concave cauterization in the shape of a nail head, which should be made of iron and the size required to fit entirely around the claw, as well as being thin-walled.
And place the heated cauterization on the nail and rotate your hand with the cauterization around the circumference of the nail until the cauterization reaches the depth of the nail. Leave it for three days until pus begins to appear. Apply a plaster made of crushed wild mustard mixed with salt to it, and leave the plaster on it for a night, as this will exterminate its roots.
Treat the area with tender generating flesh until it is healed.
If it does not improve and other observances occur on the surface of the body, particularly in the more important areas such as the chest or feet, then you must administer cauterization with water, which means you take a spoon (cucurbita) or needle or nail and place it over the claw; and apply a little hot water to the spoon, keep your hand, and rotate it around the spoon with compression of your hand from all sides, pressing the edge of the spoon against the root of the nail, and allow the hot water to flow through the root of the wound; wait for the patient for an hour for the water boil to subside, then remove it, as the claw and its roots will be exterminated.
Do the same with these and the others until you have treated all those in the body.
Treat the pus that results from the roots of the nails being exterminated with what generates flesh, which is what causes the flesh to grow in.
Chapter XXXIII.
Cauterization for tremors.
When tremors occur due to friction on the nerve or fever caused by friction, or for any similar cause, then it is necessary that you cauterize it with four cauterizations or five on the spinal column, between each spinal vertebra there should be one cauterization; in the feet, and on the stomach, use olive oil as a cauterization.
And the tremor of it subsides, and hastens the healing of the frigid disease.
Chapter LV.
Cauterization for accidents involving ulcers on the body.
When ulcers or pustules appear on the body, and are made of gross, corrupted materials; then at the beginning when it appears, it is necessary to cauterize over the entire fistula with a thin cauterization made of myrtle wood, the end of which is extended by fire; or with a long razor from erestology; or with a slow cauterization.
And at certain times, the cauterization is applied at the beginning of its expulsion according to this method; and it is not believed that it is destroyed, but rather, it is ruptured, making them heal from it.
However, it should be done with appropriate evacuation by phlebotomy.
Chapter LVI.
On the cauterization of fluxes of blood caused by an accident through the incision of an artery.
At certain times, flux of an artery that is cut must be stopped by sewing the wound closed, or the incision of a postemate (a surgical opening to evacuate pus) or cauterization of the member, and then it seems so, but it is difficult to prevent its return.
Therefore, when it happens to someone, you should immediately tie it with your hand at the opening of the artery and press on it until the flux of blood stops within a certain number of moments so that it does not come out again.
Then press the olive oil cauterizers (a tool used for cauterization) few and large, by name, and exhale on them until they are hot.
Then take one of them, either small or large, according to the place and the wound where the artery is broken, on that vein as quickly as possible after stopping the blood flux, and cauterize it until it is sealed and stopped the blood flow.
And if the blood is expelled from the wound of the artery when you stop the blood flux and withdraw the cautery, then take another cautery cautiously from those in the fire that have been prepared, and do not cease this until the blood flow is stopped.
And be careful not to burn the nerves that are here, and let another evil come upon the patient.
And know that when the artery fluxes blood, it is not possible to stop the blood in those cases, and especially when the artery is large, unless by one of four methods: either with cauterization as previously mentioned, or extraction when it has not been extracted, because when the extremities are burned and the blood flow is stopped, or by being tied with thread or by strong ligature, or by placing medications on it that have the property of stopping the blood; and they should be strengthened with pulvinar (a surgical instrument) or compression in a decent manner.
However, the one who applies a decent ligature with thread and strong compression with cloth or by heating the causes and similar ones should not be trusted completely.
However, if this happens to someone who is not a doctor or does not have medication present, then close the wound on that vein as previously mentioned, and be aware of the great caution required until the blood flow is stopped from the upper part of the wound, and the artery should not be touched; and over the artery it should be sprinkled with cold water of great coolness until the blood is coagulated and thickened; and moreover, sew where cauterization or medicine is necessary.

First Chapter.
On the treatment of water, which is contained in the head of infants.
Know that this disease often occurs in infants, and when the newborn girl has difficulty passing through the head of the infant with her head.

And this humidity can be added between the scalp and the bone, or it can be added below the bones at the fontanel (the soft spot on an infant's skull).

And another method of incision is to consider the size of the abscess and the collection of water, because sometimes it is larger in the occipital region, or in front, or on the left, or on the right; therefore, pay attention to the incision where the abscess and the accumulation of water appear, and do what is most possible for you.

Second Chapter.
When the cataracts or tumors occur on the eyes or feet, and it is an old custom that does not confer healing through medications, then the last resort in this case is the incision of those two auricles (arteries).

This operation is better than any other and more convenient.

Title VII.
On the treatment of auricle excision (removal).
Some warts grow out of the bellies of the elderly men without perforating, and this condition sometimes occurs in some men, an excision in the auricle's tissue due to a wound or lack of tissue at that site; and this excision is sometimes performed in the area before the ear lobe that does not heal, and sometimes it is outside of the partitions.
The one that occurs in the area before the ear lobe that does not heal is more difficult to cure.
And in the one where healing occurs, you should keep the patient's wart on the sole and watch it. Therefore, if an excision is observed to have healed, open that with a thin spatula in this form:
If the area to be excised has a small width and one side is sharp and the other is not; and the spatula should be two leopard lengths wide so that it does not damage the wart.
And if the excision is due to tissue born in the auricle or its surrounding area, then make a shallow and wide incision, cutting through the tissue as quickly as possible while leaving all the tissue intact.
And if the excision is in the area before the auricle, take a thin wire a lion's length and heat it slightly with fire, then place it in the auricle tissue.
And if you observe an excision with what the patient experiences relief, because of pain, release the pressure on it with ease; and be careful not to injure the nerves of the auricle.
Then you place a linen cloth on the excised area according to the size of the wound that you have wrapped in Egyptian balm; and do this for several days until you are sure of the healing of the wound; or take some herb and place it in warm water and grind it, then apply it as a poultice and use it; and if you see the excised area already healed, then you must remove the herb and replace it with another that you will wrap in beeswax that has been made with rose oil, until the cauterized wound is healed; and take care of it until it is cured.
But if there is bleeding, immerse sponge or cloth in warm water and place it on the excised area, and use the other treatment that stops the bleeding, which is called in the distillation treatise.
Title VIII.
On the care of athazel, which affects the eyelids.
Athazel is sometimes moist and other times dry in the eyes.
Therefore, you must have them with tweezers or scissors, and cut them with the spatula of their roots, and place a poultice on them as described above.
But if pain with bleeding occurs, you cauterize them with a fine lancet cautery.
The best cauterization is near the incisions and when the wounds heal properly, they do not return; and when cauterized with fire, the roots are burned and they do not return.
Title IX.
Treatment of swelling that occurs in the eyelids of humans.
Some causes that resemble swelling in the eyelids of humans are characterized by their intensity and duration, and because of this swelling, they are called swellings.
It is an accumulation of thick moisture in the eyelid above and below.
Therefore, the operation is that you examine if the swelling is increasing in the area appearing from the eyelid and spreading all over; and the cause of it is light.
Therefore, make an incision in the swelling with a scalpel and remove it from all sides with ease until it drains, and then suspend it with a hook and cut off the affected area.
And if the figure is large, then adjust it with stitches; and take care of it until it heals.
And if it is small, you will not suffer harm from the puncture since the heat of it restores and fills it in.
And if the swelling is decreasing within the eyelid, then shave the area inside the eyelid, and lift the swelling with a hook, one that you do not need to incise, and press it from all sides, and if the eyelid is elongated due to an incision, you will not notice any effect.
Then make the incision, wash the wound with salt water; and take care of it until it heals.
Chapter X.
Treatise on the cure of an eyelid abscess.
An abscess occurring on the eyelid above, which is generated in the tunica of the eyelid, especially in children, worsens the eyes of those and contributes to their catarrh more; and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears flow into them.
And you often find them on the cheeks all the time, and they sleep with their faces on their cheeks; and the underside of their eyelids is moist, which has already been inflamed, and the imminence of infection is apparent in the eye; and whenever you press the area with your fingers, you feel pus coming out into them.
And there is some method of operation in the one where the patient bends their head towards you and lays a piece of cloth over it, and boil water, and make a circle according to the amount that contains arsenic on all sides, and place that over it and press it with your fingers all around so that pus is accumulated in the middle of the circle, and then make an incision in the middle of the moisture at the wound and the wound should not be larger than the wound made during a lanceotomy.
But in the former case it is necessary that you cut open the wound completely until you reach the pus, because in the most serious cases, pus will be drained through an incision according to the shape of white cheese.
Therefore, you remove it with cloths that you have wrapped between your fingers on the sides and turn it between your right and left hands until it is dispersed.
And be careful not to close the incision because with pus you will not reach the eye and damage it.
But if pus does not appear at the beginning of the incision, but you notice that it is present in the incision, then close a small part of the incision with ease until pus appears; and remove it as I have said; submerge cloths in water and wipe it and place them on the area and tighten them with powders.
And also, those who suffer from salt and wipe it in the concavity of the incision to remove what remains of the moisture.
And take care of it until it heals.
But if an abscess occurs in the cauterized area, then take care of it with approved plasters until it heals.

Methods of touching the eye.

Then draw an arch over both lines that you have marked, and start from the greater lacrimal to the lesser one. And if your incision is near the natural furrow as is the thickness of a coin.

If you wish, leave the wound unsutured, and treat it with something that dries and constricts, because the eyelid is swollen due to the sealing of the wound and its accumulation; however, stitching is better, and therefore the ancients preferred this.
However, it should be cautioned for the patient, and it is a good action, and there is no need to fear.

Sometimes hairs grow into the eyelid, so it is necessary to use what has been said about incision; however, stitching is more artificial.
Treat with reeds in this way: and you turn the eyelid and cut the figure inside as I have described; then take two reeds or fine sticks whose length is the same as that of the eyelid and the width of them is smaller than that of the wound. Capital .13.
Of the treatment of this eyelid swelling that is above.
When the eyelid swells, and it is contraction of the eyelid when it is contracted on top, either right or left side, due to poor consolidation of a plague or section or burn, and it is called leprosy, and this swelling is natural or accidental, and it is caused by consolidation of a plague or sections or burns, or similar to their bad care.

Chapter XVI.
On incision of nails and removal of the prominence of caruncle tissue.
Know that nails are of two types: either they are nervous and resemble hard, subtle matter; or they are non-nervous, similar to white, congealed moisture. When you touch it with a probe, it collapses and is separated from the probe without being implanted in it.
And both types do not start until the larger tear duct covers part of the vision and prevents light and movement of the eye.
However, the method of working on the incision is that the patient bends their head towards you and opens their eyes, and you lift the eyelid with your hand, collect the nail with a probe of moderate length and extend it to the incisions above. Then take a needle and pierce through a hair from the horse or ox or cow, or similar animal, or strong iron, or double the tip of the needle little by little and insert it into the middle of the nail, and penetrate it with the needle, and remove the nail; extend it to the incisions above, and excise the hair around the edge of the nail that touches the pupil. And in this way, you follow the hair towards the end of the incision.
Then you incise the remnant of the tear duct at its root with a thin spatula or small scissors, and excise the natural tissue of the tear duct so that continuous flow of tears is not caused by the incision of it.
And at times the nail with only the tip extended or removed, as mentioned above, should be excised with a lion's hair spatula, which is its shape.
And take care that the spatula does not touch the corneal tissue and causes a rupture, and that the pupil is perforated.
Make the incision in the eyelid with a little bit of salt or lime made from cinnabar, and leave it for a day, and take care of it with water that should be applied until it is healed.
And if the nail is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle into it or it collapses with the probe, this type of nail should be cured with medications, and healed in the same way as described above and recommended in the division.
And if you want to incise it, you open the patient's eye and take a thin lion-shaped spatula with sharpness as follows: with fineness. And if it is rarefied and contracted and enters the tear duct, you distill your own oil of rosin made from sulphur or rosin or salt-water, and place it in the eye for another day.
And approach the operation repeatedly until everything that is from it has passed, unless the counter-abscess appears in the eye, in which case you should excise it, and treat the abscess at the beginning until it is healed.
And approach your operation repeatedly over it with reason until it is healed.
The prominence of tear duct tissue, if noticed in the eye due to harm, should be stopped with a probe; and incise it from one side, without extending the incision so that tears do not flow.
And approach distilling oil of rosin made from sulphur in the eye until it is healed.
Chapter XVII.
On incision of ingrown hair and what is born of skin attached to the eyelid.
Sometimes in the heels of some people, raw flesh is born and swells up until it covers the pupil or approaches or presses on the eyelids and strongly compresses the eyelids at the outer corners and resembles a rose-bush balustrade.

Use the incision that you will make or use the spatula that we have recommended in toenail incision, or small forceps with which you can grasp the nail as appropriate according to this chapter.
Since your incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, you fill the heel with saltpeter or distill it into red powder similar to that of corrosive medicines, and place it on the heel covered with alum until it is certain that the wound is cauterized.
If there is any cause of inflammation and the wound cauterizes blood, and you fear that it will become cauterized, you must lance the heel and treat the cauterization with whatever causes it to subside, and then apply the operation until it heals, and do the same for the surrounding skin affected by this type of inflammation.
However, you must ensure that the healing of the heel occurs naturally or by accident, and do not put your hand in any of these operations until you see that the member has suffered enough from this operation.

Capital XIX
On the reduction of arising nosebleeds.

It is called a sharp-headed instrument, made of iron and rounded like an ass's head that is pierced by a punch with a small hole (such as shown in the following form).
Place it on the corrupt area of the bone, and turn it with your fingers until it is rotated, and press gently until you know that the corruption has been removed.
Let it be done for several observations, and then restore the area with drying and stiffening agents.
If the area is consolidated and good flesh has grown there and it is separated from the body for 40 days without being renewed or developing an abscess or any accident happening, then you will know that it is healed.
If not, do not be deceived but rather reduce the fracture to the shape of the nose, and proceed as follows: First, you should discover the bone using forceps or acute medicine, and when the bone is exposed, you take three pieces as shown below:

Capital XX
On the reduction of the swelling of the nose.
When the nose swells completely and no harm or diminution occurs from this, you should make the patient lie down and follow these instructions: keep them quiet without strain or injury and use good suction; apply a linen poultice to the swelling that is made of catnip, aloe, elder, and colocynth, and strengthen the bandage over the nose without powder.
The method for the powders is to take fourfold strips of lion's wool and make powder from them.
Then place one on top of another according to the amount that the patient needs. Strengthen one over the other with a thick and strong binding, then apply cupping glasses with suction without cutting, and remove the cupping glasses and let the wound heal during the day and night.
But if the ligament becomes softened in the meantime, then it must be tied more tightly.
Then return the ligament during the day and night as previously stated.
If the wound has already been reduced (healed), that is good; if not, continue applying the plaster, powder, binding, and cupping until it is healed.

Capital XXIV.
From the healing of flesh, do not take anything in the nose.

Capital thirty (XXX)
Extraction of teeth.
It is necessary to care for the tooth from its pain with all care and patience throughout the entire extraction process, because it is not a good thing that you leave behind the root when it is extracted, as it is a superficial substance until it is excavated during the extraction process.
Furthermore, when the patient is to extract that tooth in pain, it is important that you are certain which tooth is causing the pain, because many times the pain deceives the patient and causes them to believe that the healthy tooth is causing the pain, and you remove the healthy one instead of the painful one. The pain will not cease until the diseased and painful tooth has been removed, as we have already seen in barber surgery.
Therefore, since you must be certain which tooth is causing the pain and know it well, you should then score around the tooth with a spatula containing some medicine, until the tooth is dissolved from the gum on all sides, and apply it gently using tweezers or fine forceps, starting with a small movement, continuing until you have reached the desired goal.
Apply oil or ointment with strong holders and large tweezers for good grip or strong structure, and support the patient's head between your thick fingers so that you do not hurt it, and carefully move the tooth in a manner that does not break it or cause the patient more pain.
And therefore, if the above steps are followed, you should then take one of those instruments and place it near the tooth with ease and effort, removing it as was done at the beginning.
However, if the tooth is broken or corroded, it is necessary that you wrap it with cloth and tighten it at the root end using fine wire to prevent it from being crushed during your compression on it.
It is necessary that you work carefully with scoring around the entire circumference of the gum and use caution to avoid breaking it and leaving it fractured, and return to the patient for the worsening pain that may be greater than the initial pain they had.
And remember that you should not do what some ignorant barbers do in their procedures and audacity with tooth extraction, because they do not administer what has been recommended; for many times they cause great pain in the sick person, which are difficult to be relieved, and all or some of the roots remain, or the tooth is extracted along with bone fragments from the jaw as it has been shown in many cases.
And during the extraction process, wash the mouth with warm water or saltwater.
If bleeding occurs during this procedure, such as in many cases, you should first apply some vinegar or vinegar-soaked cloth to the affected area, and if it does not stop the bleeding, cauterize.
The shape of the fine forceps and tweezers used for extracting the tooth at the beginning should be long in length, short in width, and thick, to prevent them from being bent when working with them.
They should be of such a size that the handles are not bent when gripped firmly, but rather have short lengths.
Iron bands of India, properly made and correctly applied on the outside, have teeth on them that enter into each other and tighten with strong constraint. Sometimes the area where these bands are applied has the shape of a stork's beak, which is called "guanta," and they exert great constriction.

Chapter XL.
This is where the summary of the sermon on abscesses and their incision comes to an end.
Abscesses are of many species, in many ways, as remembered from their occurrence, and each is described in this book.
And they are diverse in the perforation and incision of them through two ways, of which one is by the species of abscesses themselves; and by pressing on the humors.
And the second method is for those places where accidents of the body occur, because an abscess that occurs in the head is another than one that occurs in the anus; and the abscess that occurs in the flesh is another than one at a joint; and to each of them there is its own treatment by operation.
Furthermore, some abscesses require that they are not perforated unless the pus matures in them or their completion occurs.
Other abscesses require that they be drained when they are hard and have not matured according to their completion, such as the abscesses that occur at joints, because an abscess that is near a joint extends until it reaches the surrounding tissues or nerves of that joint, which causes contraction of the affected member; or is an abscess on a main organ and if you delay the perforation of it until it has matured it will damage the main organ; or is one in the anus, therefore you should not perforate an unripe one; and you should not perforate hard ones unless there is no digestion completed, but rather the one that is on the anus, because if you do not perforate it soon enough it can penetrate into the cavities inside the anus and become a fistula or be made near its edge so that it does not heal. Furthermore, you must know the time for draining the abscess, and this is when it has matured.
And you know that it is matured when the pain subsides and the fever ceases, and an increase in the swelling and pulse decrease, and the sharpness of the abscess head, and other signs.
And because you must know that draining should be performed in the lowest place near the abscess and from where the pus flows during treatment of the swelling.
And draining is sometimes through the length of the flesh or body if abscesses are in the armpits or feet, and in the joints, ligaments, nerves, arteries; and finally, in all places that are not reflected; because in those where it is reflected, use the method according to that member.
Furthermore, when the abscess is in the flesh, it is better to perform draining after confirmation of digestion of it according to its completion, as we have said; because if you perforate it before, the body swells and is full of pus, and the lips are hardened and deep.
Other abscesses should be drained according to the depth of the flesh or body depending on the need, or according to what the affected member requires.
And you must make a small incision in the abscesses, and a large and wide or many incisions according to the variety of the size of the abscesses.
And other abscesses are those in which the wound must be concave and incised when it is done in such a way that bread and cheese can be placed on it, like one that occurs in double or bubo tumors.
And of those who are incised with a section, there are three angles; and of these is the one that is incised similarly as a figure of myrtle leaf, as in abscesses from gout.
And of those who receive round and crescent sections, they are similar to these.
But for one who is not like shallow lion abscesses, you must perforate it with a superficial perforation or just plainly.
And when the abscess is large and has collected pus, perforate it but do not be hasty to remove all the pus in that moment; having removed part of it, leave the abscess for another day, then remove a larger part, and apply warm poultices according to the degree until it is forgotten.
Moreover, if the patient is a child, woman in labor, or an elderly person in decline, for their animal spirit moves frequently and resolves pus with its exit, and the patient may die quickly as a result, so treat them carefully.
Be careful with this chapter, and when you perform the perforation for these abscesses, make sure to clean the wound and consider whether the wound of the abscess is small or a simple incision; in that case, use one of the remedies from ancient times. But if the abscess is large, and the fissures of the perforation are many, you must be careful not to push too hard until they meet.
If a part of the skin is detached from the abscess or you have created a concavity in its circumference, you must close it with old linen or thread made of cloth similar to when you treat bread or razors, without moisture; and leave it for three days; then process it and care for it with remedies that require gargling until it is healed.
But if bleeding occurs during your operation, administer warm water and wine on a cloth and place it over the area of the blood flow for a while until the bleeding subsides.
But if the bleeding persists, you must administer treatment and care and apply powders that I have recommended in multiple locations of this book and section.
But if it is winter, and the location of the abscess is near many nerves, you must apply powder in vinegar and hot oil and leave them on the area.
And if it is summer, and the locations are fleshy, you must leave powder in warm water or vinegar and oil, and all of this should be heated until the third day as we have said, and then you must remove the abscess and clean it and provide care for it with remedies suitable for it until it is healed.
And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses universally, but as I have already said in a different way, according to the distinction made for each type of abscess, the cure for it will be described in separate chapters.

Chapter 12.
On the treatment of protrusion of the navel.
Protrusion of the navel is caused by various factors; either due to a fissure in the cicaph (which is on the abdomen), with the intestine or hernia protruding as it does in other ruptures; or due to bleeding from a vein or artery, as previously mentioned, or due to compressed ventosity within.
But if it is due to a fissure in the cicaph and the protrusion of the intestine, the color of the abscess resembles that of the body; there is no pain, but it appears in various ways. If it is due to herniation of the intestine, place its location with that which has been mentioned earlier, but with much more diverse symptoms; and when you press on it with your fingers as previously advised, it becomes concealed again; and strong pain occurs at the location itself, and it must be intensely bathed and vigorously massaged.
But if it is due to moisture, there is no pain and it does not become concealed when you press with your hand, nor does it contract or increase in size.
And if it is due to bleeding, the abscess appears darkening in color and descending.
But if it is due to rotten flesh, the abscess is serious, large and hard, and it is filled according to a certain quantity.
But if it is due to ventosity, touching it does not cause pain.
And the procedure is to consider if protrusion of the navel is due to bleeding from an artery, a vein, or ventosity; in this case, you must be cautious about treating it because there is fear and dread as previously mentioned in the chapter where abscesses caused by arteries and veins were discussed.
If protrusion of the navel is due to the intestine or hernia, you must command the patient to lie on their side and remain extended; then grasp around the entire umbilicus, and command them to be facing towards you with their hands on either side; then circle the area around the umbilicus with a thin linen band over the location that you have marked with the probe; then extend the abscess's size towards its upper part using force or a scissors in a suitable manner.
And then cut the middle of the extended abscess on the linen and insert your fingers into it as indicated and try to grasp the intestine; if you have not found or protected it with the linen, then you extract any excrement and force the intestine towards the inside of the abdomen.
And if you have found the linen (or cloth), then take a small amount of oil; cut away the excess from it.
Mays si es contrario al tejido o venosa, entonces rodea ese lugar y regresa a tu operación; luego toma dos agujas y coloca en ellas dos flejes fuertes y mete dos agujas en el circuito que has hecho alrededor del absceso en manera de cruz, las cuales haces penetrar; luego fuerza el absceso en cuatro partes sobre las agujas.
Más si quieres, retire las agujas y permite que la carne se extienda y caiga por sí; o corta el lugar delgado e permita curarse con un suelo que cubra hasta que se haya sanado.
Si la protuberancia del ombligo es de carne mala o por humedad, entonces debes cerrar el absceso tal como se ha dicho y extraer la sangre o la humedad que se encuentra allí, la cual absorbe en el lugar, y luego cura este con un suelo que lo cubra y que consolide la zona.
Capítulo XXXIII
Sobre el tratamiento del cáncer.
Se ha dicho en el capítulo anterior sobre los tipos de cáncer y en qué forma es la mejor manera de tratarlo con medicinas, y que es importante cuidar no dejarla ulcerar; se había dicho que el cáncer se produce en la madre o en la cautela de su tratamiento.
Y dicen los antiguos que alguna vez el cáncer puede ser eliminado en ciertos lugares donde es posible su extirpación, como en el pecho o la cara y de allí similares en otros miembros, especialmente cuando comienza pequeño.
Pero cuando el cáncer se ha vuelto grande y ya no es posible curarlo, no debes preocuparte por él, porque yo nunca pude sanar de este ni he visto a otro hacerlo, ni que lo hayan logrado alguien.
Y la operación en ese lugar, como se ha dicho, es que debes prepararte y acompañar al paciente y purificarlo de la colera negra algunas veguadas, y luego hervir el sagrado si está contaminado evidentemente.
Y prepara al paciente con la preparación en la que se haya localizado la operación, y prohíbies los instrumentos quirúrgicos que deben estar presentes; y asegura que todo el equipo esté bien limpio hasta que no quede ninguna razón para las razones de su ocurrencia. Permítale que fluya la sangre y no hagas abscesiones ligeras de él; presiona los lugares y limpia la sangre gruesa con tu mano o el instrumento con el que puedes acceder a ellos.
Más si te contrariega el flujo de sangre gruesa en la incisión de una vena o de una arteria, entonces cauteriza aquella hasta que se detenga el flujo de sangre y luego cura esta con otra curación hasta que se haya sanado.

Then you grab the peritoneum of the testicles at each side, and with that extend the white cephalic on the sides with your left hand, and elevate the hernia sac to the incision site with the cephalic; and command the assistant to stretch out the hernia sac in front of you and you dissolve the adhesion that is behind it with a complete solution.
And look for any cause of the intestine being enclosed in the hard white cephalic. But if you find a cause for it, then you open the abdomen to examine it.
Then insert through the incision made below the cord of the testicles, where blood and pus will run out as we have recommended in what we have said.
Then apply wool soaked in oil to the wound and wait; then apply the linen bandage that we have recommended (and sometimes a white cord is cauterized, which we said should be placed near the incision to prevent blood flow, since this often happens), and leave the bandage in place until it falls off by itself.
But if the pain persists, then boil water and soak a cloth in it, and place it on the affected area until it falls off as we have said.
Then care for the wound with another treatment for wounds until it heals.

Chapter LXIX.
Castration.
You should know that castration is forbidden in our law, but I bring it up in this book because it is relevant; and its remembrance is only necessary in two cases: the first is when a doctor needs to know about it due to his knowledge of its cure when it occurs; and the second reason is when we have had necessity of castration of other animals for our uses, such as horses, cows, pigs, and similar animals.
And so I say that castration is done in two ways: by strangulation or by incision.
But in the method done by strangulation, the procedure is to restrain the animal in hot water until its genitals soften and hang down. Then grasp them with your hand inside so that they do not reappear afterwards.
But in castration done by incision and cutting, you must hold the animal and press the scrotum of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie up the suspenders and make an incision through each hole until two holes have appeared.
And then make an incision on those (testicles) that you have cut off. Do not leave any cause for the bladder in it, but remove the bladder that is near the vessels.
This method of castration is better done by strangulation, because strangulation lessens the likelihood that the testicles will be desired by the animal.
Then take care of the wound until it heals.
Chapter LXX (70).
On the cure of hermaphrodism.
In men, hermaphrodism occurs in two ways: one is when there appears a gap between the scrotum of the testicles, where there is a figure like a female vagina with hair.
And sometimes it also occurs that the urine passes from the scrotum of the testicles.
But in women, it is a special case: and it is that the vagina of the woman over the cervix is like two testicles of a man, but much smaller, like the foreskin of a man and two testicles.
And the cure is of three types: two for men and one special type for women. It is necessary to incise the affected tissue and remove the pressure from there, and take care of it with other treatments for other diseases.
In the second type of men who have urine in their scrotum, there is neither cure nor action to be taken on it.

Chapter .lxxii.
On the treatment of scrofula.
Scrofula is when the woman's neck is not perforated or small. And it can be natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to disease that has occurred before, and it is caused by excess flesh or a subtle or thick cyst.
It can be made in the mother's womb, on her ribs, or on the upper or lower part of her body, and prohibit coit, binding, and childbearing, and strongly prohibit menstruation.
The knowledge of that (scrofula) is found by examining the mother, if the opening is obvious, it is palpable; but if it is not obvious, then you search for it with your fingers or the eye.
But if the opening is due to a subtle cyst and it is close to the labia, then you cut and tear it apart.
And place your fingers on both labia, and place your fingers close to the opening, then search for it more deeply later.
The woman should be on her back, her legs extended, and stretch the labia apart with force until the subtle cyst is broken and the opening is open.
And take wool and dip it in oil and place it on the area, and press with a cloth for three days to ensure that the incision does not heal.
But if the cyst is large and thick, then you must cut it open with a lancet or a myrtle leaf.
But if the opening is due to a tumor, then suspend it with oil and cut it open.
And use the medications that stop bleeding without causing pain, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and ennses, mixed with alum of hops.
And provide a wide lead pipe to prevent the wound from healing lightly.
Hold it for several days and administer warm water.
And let it heal with the other healing of consolidation until it is healed.
Sometimes it happens during the mother's delivery of other fleshes, and then you must cut according to this method. But if it is due to cancerous fistula, do not make an incision in any way on the cancerous fistula of the mother.

Chapter LXXV.

Chapter LXXVI.
On the extraction of the dead child.
When you care for a dead child as we have said in the division of medicine and it is not extraneous, and you are determined to use force, then you must consider if the woman is of good virtue and not among those about whom there is fear of harm.
Then the woman should be laid on her back, with her head lowered and her legs raised.

Then the midwife should anoint her hands with those oils and emollients, then insert them into the mother's vagina with ease, and circle around the area where the fingers are inserted in the child.
Choose the appropriate location: therefore you should consider if the fetus is positioned correctly on its head, and then insert your fingers into the heels, neck, mouth, palate, below the beard, at the junction of the spine, or near the ribs, or below the hips (hip bones).
But if it is positioned on its feet, then you should insert your fingers into the crotch or the small of the back.
It is necessary to hold the finger with the right hand, and bend it in the location between the fingers of the left hand, then insert the hand with ease and place the finger into one of the locations that we have mentioned, until you reach the desired outcome.
Then place another finger next to it, or the third if necessary, in order to attract it, but not extend it along its length.
It should be done gently all around, in order that the process is alleviated as much as possible, like when removing a tooth.
It is necessary that in this process the extension is softened; and if any part of it is retained, then the midwife should anoint some of her fingers with oil and insert them expertly and rotate those parts that are retained.
If the delivery is forgotten, then the umbilical cord should be tied within a place that is closer [to the baby]; and do this until everything is delivered.
If the navel remains outside the mother and cannot be reduced by traction, then a cloth should be wrapped around it; and draw it out until everything is delivered, and cut the cord at the navel or the umbilical cord.
And in the same way, you must also do this to both hands and feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is difficulty in traction on it, or water accumulates around its head, then you must insert a spatula-like instrument called an alundat between the membranes and cut open the head and drain the water, or use an instrument with the name "alundat" to puncture it. And if the head is protruding and needs traction, you should break the waters until the moisture in the feet is drained.
But if there are no complications or difficulties, you should cut open the head as soon as it is possible for you to do so.
And if the abdominal wall is protruding or swollen, you must puncture it until the moisture inside it is drained.
But if the fetus is in its pelvis, the traction of it is easy and the direction to the mother's mouth is easy.
But if it is difficult or stuck in the abdomen and pelvis, you must draw it out with a cloth that you have wrapped around your hand, and cut open the abdomen and pelvis until the moisture inside them is drained.

If that is not possible, you should cut it into pieces and draw it out.
And do not leave any foreign matter inside the second opening (vagina).

I have once seen a woman in the womb whose child was dead, and over that fire another woman was observed to be burning, and that child was also dead. Once upon a time, there was a man who had an abscess in his navel for a long time; it swelled up until it burst open and began to emit pus.
I was called to treat him, and I treated him for a long time, but the wound did not heal.

And then I thought that they were the bones of the dead child.
So I healed the wound and extracted many bones from it, but the woman continued to live in this manner for a long time; and then a small piece of arm broke off.
I was not surprised by this, because it is known and helpful in treating what doctors administer with their hands for treatment.
On the forms of the instruments necessary to extract the child.
Form of the spiral with which the mother is opened:
This is the shape of the screw-like forceps in which the fetal limbs are held, with two prongs at each end of two rods. But this instrument should be thinner than a constrictor, and made of wood or bone.
And the diameter of each rod should be two fingers at each end, and the length of each one should be a palm and a half; in the middle of the two rods there are two adjustable rods that have already been fastened, whose length is slightly more than a palm, and the diameter of each one is three fingers or slightly more.
These two additions are meant to be inserted into the mother's mouth so that it can be opened with those prescribed movements.
Make another similar mixture that is more subtle and lighter in texture:
Make it like a plaster of ebony or boxwood, similar to forceps. But on the ends of these two additions, there are to be small holes, and the length of these additions is what equals one palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open the mother, first press the woman's belly down towards the hanging feet, and open what is between her thighs. Then place your hand on the instrument, like when using forceps, according to the depth you want to open the mother's mouth until it is wide enough for the child to pass through.

Treatment for an unperforated child's bottom (Rectal treatment).
In children who are not circumcised and whose anus is not perforated, the feces should be softened and lubricated. Therefore, the midwife should perforate this anus with her finger or, if not, perforate it with a sharp sponge and make sure she does not touch the rectum.
Then place a cloth soaked in vinegar and oil over it, and treat it with anointment until it is healed.

Treatment for fistula that causes discharge (fistulous discharge).
Fistulas that cause pus-filled nodes (abscesses) near the anus or in the space of one parturition (childbirth wound).
It is a fistula or a mass.
And when that node is old and has turned into a moist, foul-smelling white or subtle pus, some of these fistulas can penetrate.
And these penetrating ones are recognized by what comes out of them through the exit and by their foul odor; and sometimes the patient uses the evacuation, but it is very dangerous to come into contact with the worms that come out of them.
And sometimes these fistulas can penetrate into the bladder space, into the muscle of the vagina, and into the union of the cavity and neck of the bladder.
And that which is recognized as a penetrating fistula in the anus and non-penetrating fistula, it is when you place your finger in the anus, and try to insert a thin probe of wood or iron into the fistula when there is no danger.
But if there is danger in that, then you should insert a thin probe of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the probe or hair in your finger.
And if you do not feel it at all or do not obtain any cause of evacuation, worms, or foul odor as we have said, then you should know that it is non-penetrating, and you should take care in the treatment.
And when the fistula penetrates into the bladder or muscle of the vagina, the significance is clearly that it is urine from that place, and you should avoid using that area for any treatment.
But if it penetrates into the union of the cavity or into the bone and encounters pain in the area, then the sign is that the probe penetrates into it if there is no danger to the bone; and this causes pain during childbirth, which becomes purulent very quickly; and it is not valid for treatment nor is it consolidated with ointment.
And in all these penetrating fistulas, there is no cure, and the cure of those is hard work and disappointment for foolish doctors on whom it depends.
But in that which is non-penetrating and not old, healing with iron is hoped for as I have recommended to you, and what I have already proven.
And the patient should lie down between your legs and elevate his legs towards you, the thighs should be inclined towards his abdomen, and then insert a probe of lead or wood if there is no danger in the fistula into the place where the probe can be felt.
And if the patient feels pain around the neck, then you must enter your hand into the neck.

On the treatment of sores.
I have already explained in the division of the treatment of sores what is suitable for the free person, and now I will explain the treatment of those with more severe conditions and medications according to the needs.
Therefore, I say that sores are diverse according to what causes the sores and according to the location where the sores occur.
And the causes of sores are often due to injuries such as falling on stones, or cuts from a sword, or a spear, or by beating with a club, or whip, or arrow, and similar causes.
But sores that occur on the parts of the body are such as a sore that occurs on the head, neck, feet, abdomen, back, and similar to those on other body parts.
And I recommend the treatment of some sores based on this reasoning and rule for other sores.
And I will begin with simple sores on the head, for a discussion of complex sores will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say that when a simple sore occurs on the head, but it is not a fracture, you should consider: if it is caused by falling on stones or something similar and the wound has already been sewn up (stitched) and is large and there is concern about an abscess developing in the patient, then immediately lance (open) the cephalic vein (the largest vein in the head), and do not delay it; and let blood flow out according to the strength of the medicine, unless there is any cause prohibiting venous lancing, especially if the blood that comes out of the sore is scant.
And the lancing should be on the opposite side of the affected area; and ensure the patient is kept away from food, drink, and heavy meals.
But if any cause forbids the patient from eating, then reduce their food and do not give them meat or wine.
Wait on the sore if an abscess forms, cover it with rose oil or wine that has been treated with astringents (a substance used to tighten tissue and reduce inflammation).
But if you are certain that an abscess has formed, then wait on the sore, if it is recent with fresh blood and the air has not changed the powder I will recommend using a small amount of.
And if the air has already changed [i.e., passed], then wait over certain wounds until they are healed.
But if the wound is large or caused by incision of space and not properly closed with lips, then close it with stitching according to what I will recommend regarding stitching them.
But if the wound has exposed the bone and flesh, and is not held in place except for a small support, then incise it and care for the wound with medicines and restore the flesh to its original location, and instruct the patient to eat foods that are rich in groats: oats and similar grains, until it is healed.
And if the flesh decays and does not adhere to the bone, then you incise everything there and clean it, and care for it.
But if in these wounds it is an artery or vein from which bleeding may occur and has not been separated by medicines, then you explore the artery, and if that unincised artery is decayed, you incise it with a lance or a probe; and if it is necessary for what I have said to not conform, then you cauterize until the blood is separated.
And if these wounds are simple and small, their cause is light; therefore, sprinkle this powder on them, as it solidifies before the air changes them.
The method of the powder is as follows: mix one part olive oil, two parts dragon's blood oil, three parts not-extinct herbs; grind everything and sieve it, fill the wound with it, and tightly bind it with good constriction until it adheres to the bleeding, and coagulate it with the blood.
Then apply a thick layer of pulverized material over it and let it dry, and do not loosen it until it is healed, as the medicine will not be absorbed into it before it is healed.
And sometimes you perform cautery alone, when olive oil and dragon's blood are not present with you.
Now perform this method of treatment on large wounds when it is necessary to wait over them and tighten them, and on recent wounds with their blood, which the air has not yet altered.
And if the air has already altered them, especially during the summer months, do not apply this powder to that position, but instead care for those wounds with what I have said, allowing some wounds to heal on their own, or allowing those wounds coated with lime plaster to heal; and treat those with other remedies until they are healed.
But if it is a broken bone wound, which is small, you extract it with forceps.

But if the wound occurs in the neck, there is no difference in treatment from the simple head wound.

If it is not deep and the wound is recent with fresh blood, then you pause in that place for the first hour with powder, and do not press it to prevent the blood from being retained in the depth of it and returning to the heart and causing the patient pain, but rather pause on a soothing attractant, and dissolve it twice a day.

But if the healing of the wound is delayed and it remains open for a long time, then you should know that a fistula has been made; so cure it according to its own chapter.

On wounds of the abdomen.
The disorder that occurs in the abdomen may be large, small or medium-sized.
A small disruption is difficult to repair in another way, and it is known that the reduction of them is more difficult if you do not take care of their insertion back into their place quickly, as they swell and thicken making the insertion difficult.
And therefore, the best type of hernia is medium-sized, because in that case it is not difficult to reduce the intestine, unlike the two types mentioned above (large and small).
And you should know that stitching the abdomen is done according to four methods, but two of them are common and are used in stitching other wounds on the body.
And two other methods are specific to other wounds, but they are more specifically used in abdominal stitching.
I recommend that you expose and explain this matter (the treatment of hernias) to everyone.
Thus say that when the wound is small and there is a cause of the intestine due to it, and it is difficult to reduce the intestine, this is in one of two ways: either because of the small size of the hernia as we have said before, or because inflammation of the intestine has come from the cold air.

And sometimes it happens that this [affliction] is found in which there is stiffness, and it is better to use water alone for its resolution.
And therefore you wet the intestine with water containing alum and mallow, since by this the inflammation is relieved little by little.
But if the inflammation is spreading and the intestine is protruding from its place during this treatment, then you should make a small incision with an instrument for this purpose using scissors.
The initial treatment is better when it is not cut, and it is not necessary to make an incision unless absolutely required due to lack of other remedies.
Of the instrument, take its shape:
The sharp angle of the tool should be acute, while the other angle should not be blunt, and the tip should be fine but not too thin, with a slight obtuse angle.
And so when the wound is enlarged and the intestine comes out, its reduction should be in a way that follows its natural shape, in its proper place, if possible on top of it, as this is better.

And for small wounds, prepare what you need and ensure that the assistant is among your most trusted ones, who will hold the hernia with their hand and adjust the edges of it, and also cover one over the other to prevent any cause of separation during suturing.
This is the common method of suturing: Take an awl, or a needle according to the size of the wound; then hold it with the tip of the hernia, but do not insert the thread into both ends of the needle, instead take one end and leave the other free, so that you do not place the knot on the inside of the edges, until you pass it through the other side; once you have added two ends of the thread and the ends of the skin, it will be four orders.
Then strengthen the thread with a double knot around the needle, sometimes from both sides together, and bring the two edges and the wound together by appropriate tension; then let go of the thick part and insert another needle through it, and tie it in the same way as the first needle; do not stop until all the contraction of the wound has been completed with the needles.
And needles should be neither too thin nor too thick, as very thin needles easily penetrate the flesh; and thick ones are difficult to pass through the skin, so they must be of medium thickness.
And the needle should not be inserted into both edges of the adjacent skin too much, so that the flesh is not easily penetrated and the wound heals before its consolidation.
And do not prolong the suturing to prevent the wound from consolidating.
And insert the tips of the needles so as not to irritate the patient while they sleep; and place pulvils expanded on all sides over the suturing, which will hold the tips of the needles; leave them in until you know that the wound has consolidated.
And this type of suture with needles in the method described is more suitable for small wounds, as it can handle the suturing of one or several needles around them.
But the second method of suturing is common: and it consists of applying four edges, two from the skin and two from the underlying tissue, at once, using a needle that has both ends tied in thickness and fineness.
And when the needle has penetrated these four edges, withdraw it slowly from that side of the wound where you started, to draw out the thread subcutaneously around the wound, so that the stitching is similar to sewing fabric, with the threads reinforced.
And pause between each stitch the amount of thread required for the knot.
And this suture is known to men.
And with this suture, I closed a wound that had occurred in a man's abdomen, who was injured by a sword, and the hernia was larger than a palm, and it was near two palms from the intestine of the same location and was located in the middle of the member; and after 24 hours, I reduced it after the intestine had been out of the wound.

And of the signs of the servant is when it catches in it (the patient) a splinter, pierces the bone, and exits from the cavity which is above the brain, because this happens due to violent soda, scotomia, vertigo, heat in the veins, inflammation and heat of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, vomiting of bile, and the word is forcefully separated and destroyed, and exits from the wound location a whitish pus-like fluid resembling powder, and eyes from it resemble the moisture of the flesh.

But the signs of a splinter that has entered the heart, near the left breast, and is firmly embedded, are not in vain; and its movement is similar to the movement of the thumb, and there is bleeding from the wound, oozing black pus, and this heat of the limbs, sweating, and faintness; and therefore, know that death approaches quickly.

And if the splinter catches in the bladder and is discharged through urine, and causes some injury outside, there will be severe pain on the patient, know that it is deadly.
But other members, such as the head, neck, throat, back, shoulders, and adjutorium, spine, furcula, pelvis, hip, thighs, and their similar limbs are saved if the splinter does not touch a vein or artery and is not poisonous.
And I recommend to you that I have seen the nature of these splinters, so you may understand from this concerning your treatment.
The cause is that when a splinter enters the lacrimal duct of a person's eye through the nasal cavity, and it is extracted from the other side, taking care to remove the eyelash along with it, it heals, and no harm comes to the eye.

The quality of the bloodletting at that location is such that you tighten the hand with a strap or your own, then immerse it in warm water until the vein swells and is clearly visible; perform the venesection transversely; if you incise it completely, it will not be noticeable.
Be careful not to cut off your hand with the venesection, as nerves are exposed there without flesh.
Then put your hand in warm water and let the blood flow out of it, because if you do not immerse it in warm water, the blood will coagulate at the vein opening, and bleeding is forbidden.
Draw the blood according to your need, and then pause over the olive oil and salt vein so that it is not hardened; similarly, you must do this for all branches.
However, the advantage of venesection from the left-hand vein is that it is beneficial for gallbladder diseases.
Perform similarly in the venesection of this as you have done with the other.
The advantage of the saphenous vein venesection is for diseases in the lower part of the body such as abscesses, retention of menstruation, and lung diseases, ulcers, and old sores, and their similar conditions.
The quality of the bloodletting at that location is such that the patient inserts their foot into warm water and performs friction on it until the veins appear; then on the ankle with a strap, and the site of the vein should be pointed out, and from there, it branches out on the sole of the foot multiple ways.
